Negotiations on the Jinliyuan Case Reopened 123

The French Side Indicates a Price and Agrees to Transfer

The Jinliyuan Wharf case of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has been suspended for a long time due to the transfer of Father Xiaqi of the Sanduo Church to Korea. It is now learned that lawyer Bahe, the representative of the Sanduo Church, has submitted the wharf price to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and the two sides are conducting negotiations. The details are as follows:

Indicated Price: Lawyer Bahe sent a letter to Lawyer Gao Shuo yesterday, indicating that the Sanduo Church officially agreed to sell, but the asking price for the sale was 390,000 taels per 1.16 acres. A reply was required by the 14th of the month, otherwise a request would be made to the Municipal Council for execution.

Extension of Negotiations: General Manager Li of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company convened a meeting with Lawyer Gao Shuo to discuss the response. The response was that the deadline was too tight and serious consideration was needed. As a result, Lawyer Gao visited Consul General Gan orally at 11:00 AM yesterday to request the Municipal Council and grant a one-month extension to allow for a longer period of consideration. Lawyer Gao also told him that the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company had been transferred to state ownership and asked for consideration of Sino-French friendship and a further extension. The result was agreement.

Attitude of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: Lawyer Gao Shuo wrote a letter to Bahe to respond to the Sanduo Church and entrusted a Chinese Christian to mediate with the priest to reduce the price and schedule negotiations. In the future, the price will be based on the assessment of the Shanghai Municipal Council so that neither party will suffer.

Reply to Lawyer Bahe: I received your letter of November 3 this year from the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, delivered by your lawyer, stating that the Sanduo Church agrees to transfer all of Deed No. 69 of the Love Character to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and listing various conditions. My lawyer, in the capacity of arbitrator, represents the reply and agrees with the fundamental points of the letter. However, the conditions are of great importance and require serious consideration. We have requested the French Municipal Council to extend the deadline by one month for longer consideration. We should first reply to your lawyer for your information and to forward it to the Sanduo Church. Lawyer Gao Shuo, November 13, 19.

Water Police Planning Winter Defense 126

Will Organize Guerrilla Squadrons

According to the Kwow Min News Agency, yesterday, a reporter met with Chen Zekuan, head of the first district of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, and asked about the winter defense situation on the water in the district. A meeting was held at the beginning of this month to discuss the method, and it was decided to organize a guerrilla squad. All the teams will be selected from the existing subordinates to form two squadrons to be responsible for the guerrillas. In addition, two shallow-water warships under the district will patrol the defense zones of Chuan Nan, Song Jiang, and Fengxian counties to supplement the guerrillas. The team is currently being organized and will be completed and dispatched by the end of this month. As for the land joint defense, the Jiangsu Provincial Department has set a full plan. In case of an alarm, the water police will cooperate with it.

Thirty-Two Silk Factories Notify Female Workers 127

Reduce Wages and Maintain Operations, Willing or Not is Up to You

The thirty-two silk factories in this city that are planning to start operations sent a notice to the female workers yesterday, stating that the silk market is in decline, stocks are difficult to sell, and the cost of cocoons exceeds the selling price. The factory has been losing money for a year, so it has no choice but to temporarily suspend operations. Now, it has received a notice from the silk factory industry association, advising it to endure the pain and try to start operations for the sake of the livelihoods of the workers after a long period of closure. Therefore, it has to save costs in order to barely maintain operations. The wages of all silk reeling female workers will be temporarily calculated at 50 cents per day. All other parts will be reduced accordingly. It is up to each of the female workers to decide whether or not to come to the factory to work. The factory will not force them. This notice is hereby given for your information.

Both Railways Will Convene a Business Conference 128

After Liu Weizhi, Director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, concurrently took charge of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus, he said that the two railways run through Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces. One end is Shanghai, the largest commercial port in the country and the only port for the import of foreign goods, and the other end is the capital, which is connected to the Tianjin-Pukou and Longhai Railways in the north, and adjacent to the richest provinces of Anhui and Jiangxi in the west. One end is Hangzhou, the capital of Zhejiang Province, which will be the starting point of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and an important route for goods from the interior of Anhui. According to the location and situation, the freight transportation of the two railways should have been developed long ago. However, in the past, the executives of the two railways did not have an in-depth study of the routes of water and land transportation and the types and quantities of products along the way, nor did they have sufficient contact with local commercial banks, factories, and transit industries, so that both the railways and businesses did not benefit. Director Liu saw this, so he ordered Liu Chengchang and Zheng Baozhao, the directors of the Vehicle Department, to discuss the reorganization of the Vehicle Department and the addition of a commercial section to plan to improve the freight transportation of the two railways. Since the reorganization, it has only been five months, and the freight transportation of the two railways has gradually increased. Director Liu and others believe that this development is the initial effect of the reorganization. If the organization is further improved, the future will be limitless. Therefore, it has been decided to convene a business conference of the two railways next month to discuss all specific methods. At present, preparations are being actively made. Here is an exploration of the preparations.

Busy Preparations: Director Liu believes that this conference will directly benefit the business development of both the railway bureau and the merchants, and indirectly reduce the people's livelihood. The importance of its mission is no less than that of the financial and industrial and commercial conferences convened by various ministries. Therefore, there must be sufficient preparations before this conference. It is said that Director Liu has authorized the Vehicle Department to preside over the entire conference, so Liu Chengchang and Zheng Baozhao, the directors of the Vehicle Department, are currently very busy preparing for this matter.

Inviting Members: It is said that in addition to the directors and section chiefs of the railway bureau as natural members, the conference will invite representatives from the provincial governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, chambers of commerce from cities and counties along the way, chambers of commerce from various industries, transit companies, and transportation experts. All invitation letters will be sent out soon.

Soliciting Opinions: In addition to asking each member to submit proposals in advance or temporarily, the Railway Bureau welcomes any improvement plans for railway transportation from all walks of life. However, they must be sent to the Railway Bureau in advance for discussion at the meeting.

The Seafarers' Wage Increase Issue with Taikoo Company Resolved 133

Contract to be Signed Next Tuesday

Resolution of Seafarers' Wage Increase: After the Union repeatedly sent representatives to discuss the contract with the Taikoo Company, both parties agreed to make concessions to resolve the issue of seafarers demanding wage increases from foreign ships, which has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the Union also sent Secretary Liu Yuzhou and branch leaders Wang Yongsheng to Taikoo to discuss and revise the wording of the wage increase contract, remove the word "never," and add "Republic of China 19" (the contracts have always been written only in the Western calendar). It was stipulated that from September 1, all seamen, firemen, and stewards would receive a wage increase of four yuan per month. The Union side agreed that if the company needed assistance within the scope of the Union, it could consider the situation and provide assistance with its consent. This wage increase contract is scheduled to be signed by the representatives at the company next week. The articles are drafted by the Seafarers' General Union, one each in Chinese and Western languages. Both parties sign and each holds one copy.

Stevedores' Wage Increase Agreed: After the Union representatives negotiated on the issue of stevedores of the new Taikoo ships requesting the compradores of each ship to implement the wage increase, it was heard yesterday that the compradores of each ship had made a definite statement that they have now agreed to increase the salary of stevedores by 4 yuan per month for those who requested 6 yuan per month. The stevedores have expressed satisfaction. The issue has also reached a solution.

Chinese Red Cross Society Receives Report of War and Disaster in Suixian County Yesterday 134

Thirty-Seven Trenches, Totaling 245,700+ Feet in Length

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a report of the disaster situation in Suixian County, Henan Province, via telegram from the Henan Provincial Relief Committee, stating that the county was the center of the war zone and suffered unusually heavy losses and casualties. After a detailed investigation, it was found that there were thirty-seven trenches in Suixian County, each with a depth of more than one foot and a total length of 245,700+ feet. More than 2,700 people were killed or injured by artillery fire, 6,270+ houses were destroyed or damaged, 13,900+ horses, mules, and donkeys were lost, 1,580+ carts were lost, 1,948,000+ yuan worth of property was lost, and 100,000+ yuan in donations were levied. Also, 47,800+ people were conscripted into labor. The sight of the survivors is unbearable. Please provide immediate relief and assistance. The Henan Provincial Relief Committee, Zhang Fang, bows to the east. The association has already appealed to various places to raise funds for emergency relief.

Local News 2

### Large Batch of Heroin Continued to Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday 145

A total of 111 boxes in three shipments, worth approximately over one million yuan. The smugglers appear to be from a certain country. The third batch will continue to be inspected today.

Regarding the seizure of a large quantity of heroin worth over 200,000 yuan by the Jianghai Customs in goods transported to Shanghai on the Italian ship Koldirana, a detailed report of the matter obtained by a reporter is recorded below:

### First Seizure in Hong Kong 146

The seizure of heroin by the Jianghai Customs in Shanghai was the second such incident. The first seizure occurred in Hong Kong. Previously, the Italian Postal Shipping Company's Hai Guan Da ship, which sailed from Austria to Shanghai, arrived in Hong Kong. In late last month, the ship was loaded with 49 boxes of goods shipped from Trieste, Austria, to Shanghai. 28 boxes were marked to be unloaded in Shanghai, and the rest were to be unloaded in Dalian Bay, divided into three bills of lading. The bills of lading stated that the goods were raisins and other food. Hong Kong customs officers opened the boxes and discovered that they were all morphine, heroin, and other drugs. The value was enormous, at least 500,000 to 600,000 yuan. The goods were immediately seized because the bill of lading did not specify the consignee, so it was impossible to know the purchaser and transporter. The ship then arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong, but unexpectedly, three boxes were left on the ship that were not searched by the Hong Kong customs. After arriving in Shanghai, they were picked up by private buyers, but they had already suffered losses.

The second batch, discovered in Shanghai, was mostly shipped from Austria. The shipping point has not yet received news of the failure in Hong Kong. The second batch of goods shipped to Shanghai was only half a month apart from the first batch. The second batch consisted of 26 boxes (mistakenly reported as 36 boxes yesterday), which were still transshipped from Constantinople to China. They were divided into two batches, one with 20 boxes and the other with 6 boxes, which were handed over to the Italian Postal Ship Coldelana for transport to Shanghai. The ship entered port on the 7th. When it passed through Hong Kong on the 4th of this month, Hong Kong customs wanted to seize it, but due to time constraints, the customs officers were unable to board the ship before it set sail. They immediately sent a secret telegram to Shanghai, ordering the Jianghai Customs to be vigilant. When the Jianghai Customs sent officers to search the ship, the goods had already been picked up and placed in the Gonghexiang Wharf warehouse. Six boxes in the two batches had already been picked up by the consignee, so only 20 boxes were searched. The bills of lading and box surfaces still stated "raisins," but upon inspection, they were found to be a large amount of heroin. These 20 boxes alone weighed 2,200 kilos. Because the bill of lading did not have a consignee, the customs office seized the goods and stored them in the customs warehouse while investigating the smugglers.

The third batch arrived yesterday. The second batch had just been seized by the customs when the Italian company's ship Cracovia arrived yesterday with few goods because it was mainly carrying passengers, so there were only a few hundred items of imported goods. Unexpectedly, goods were found among them with the same packaging as the previous two batches, also transshipped from Constantinople and without the consignee's name. There were four batches, totaling 33 boxes, with a total of 3,559 kilos. The Italian Postal Company first discovered the goods upon arrival in Shanghai and ordered the ship to temporarily store the goods in the Gonghexiang warehouse and to check the bills of lading and other numbers. It was expected that the Jianghai Customs would definitely find out or would seize them. When the reporter inquired yesterday, he learned that the goods had not yet been opened for inspection by the customs office. However, since they were shipped by the original company and packaged in the same way, it could be predicted that they must be toxic substances.

Smugglers of Toxic Substances The total number of toxic substances smuggled to Shanghai this time, including those confiscated in Hong Kong, totaled 111 boxes in three batches. Nine boxes were picked up, and the total weight of the three batches was 20,665 kilos. The shipping agent in Austria was Transportlnternatilnaux, and according to the reporter's investigation, the consignee in Shanghai appeared to be from a certain country. The nine boxes that were picked up in the first two shipments were all in the name of Meishlco, which appears to be the name of a trading company from a certain country, but the address is unknown. As for the 33 boxes that arrived yesterday, some were labeled "raisins" and others "clansing material." 19 of the 33 boxes were marked for transshipment to Tianjin and Dalian. The total value of the three batches of heroin was at least 1.2 to 1.3 million yuan. This is truly the largest amount of drugs flowing into Shanghai in recent times.

### Zhabei Public Bus Strike for Four Hours 147

Cause Was a Misunderstanding with the 27th Regiment of Soldiers

From around 1 p.m. to 4 p.m. yesterday, all public buses on Zhabei's 123 Road were suspended. According to the company, at around 10 a.m. yesterday, Public Bus No. 4111 on Zhabei 1st Road was traveling from the North Station to Tongji Road on Tiantong'an Road when two soldiers from the 17th Company of the 27th Regiment wanted to board. The driver refused because it was not at a designated stop. The soldiers boarded anyway and fell off the footboard as the bus was moving, tearing their clothes. The bus continued to Jiangwan to turn around and, unexpectedly, the two soldiers had gathered a crowd and blocked the bus, throwing stones and breaking the bus windows. The driver and ticket seller were injured, and one of the passengers was also injured in the head. The others escaped. The two injured were sent to Jisheng Hospital. The doctor said that their lives could be saved if there were no complications within 24 hours. The staff on the 123 Road bus went on strike in the afternoon, citing unprovoked harassment. The Garrison Headquarters dispatched an adjutant to mediate with the Public Security Bureau. No results were achieved. At around 4 p.m., the buses resumed normal operation. The damaged bus was also driven back to the company at that time.

### Yixing Students Established a Support Association for the Xiao Case Yesterday 148

Overseas Chinese Federation Convened a General Assembly of All Circles

The Yixing Students in Shanghai Support Association for the Xiao Case was officially established at 2 p.m. yesterday at the Shanghai Law School on Jiangwan Road. More than 40 or 50 representatives of male and female students from Yixing from over a dozen universities and high schools, including Fudan, Daxia, Labor, Chizhi, Political Science, Zhonggong, Dongya Wuben, Southeast, Overseas Eastern School, Datong, Tongde, and Dongwu Law School, attended the meeting. (3) Implementation steps (proactive aspect): A. Petition to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs with seven demands: 1. The Dutch government must formally apologize to the Chinese government and various organizations. 2. Stop the Java Company's ships from operating in China. 3. The chief mate must be sentenced to capital punishment. 4. The second mate must receive appropriate punishment. 5. The doctor must be dismissed. 6. Warn the comprador He. 7. Similar cases must not occur again in the future. B. Petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters. C. Contact relevant organizations for joint action. D. Request the Japanese Newspaper Association to notify all newspapers not to publish Java Company advertisements. E. Send a letter to the Overseas Chinese Federation Xiao Case Support Association urging immediate action and requesting the convening of an enlarged meeting of all Xiao Case support associations in Shanghai. (Passive aspect): A. Send express mail and telegrams to various newspapers. B. Send a telegram of condolence to Ms. Xiao. C. Issue a declaration. The meeting adjourned at 6 p.m.

The Overseas Chinese Federation sent a letter to the Yixing students in Shanghai yesterday, stating: "Respected Teachers: The news that Ms. Xiao Xin'an, a female teacher from our country, was sexually assaulted by the Dutch first and second mates of the Java Company ship Zhibade while traveling south has caused outrage throughout the country. The Municipal Party Headquarters has also sent a letter to our association to provide unanimous assistance. As this matter concerns the public, we intend to jointly initiate the convening of a general assembly of all circles to discuss ways to support Xiao, avenge the humiliation, and alleviate the suffering of overseas Chinese in Dutch territories. The timing is urgent. We respectfully request that your association provide an early response so that we can convene and initiate the general assembly this week. We would be deeply grateful."

### Results of Negotiations in the Xin Case 149

The French Naval Authorities Have Punished the Culprits and Provided Compensation

Regarding the case in which the Shanghai sampan boatman Xin Dingxiang was pushed into the Huangpu River and drowned by two French sailors, the municipal government repeatedly negotiated with the French consul-general and demanded that the culprits be punished and compensation be provided. It is now learned that the French consul-general, Gancelin, replied to the municipal government a few days ago, stating that the case had been thoroughly investigated by the French naval authorities, and the two sailors had been detained and punished. They are currently negotiating with the family of the deceased to provide compensation and have strictly ordered that such incidents not occur again in the future. Based on this, the municipal government has also sent letters to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Shanghai District Court for reference and decided to continue strict negotiations.

### A Small Kidnapping Case in Caojiadu 150

Four-Year-Old Boy Jin Lin Went Missing and Was Redeemed for 140 Yuan. The Culprit Cao Zhigan Has Been Arrested. The Rickshaw Driver's Identification Was Unmistakable.

Jin Lin, the four-year-old son of a woman named Huang Li from Jiangbei, who resides at No. 3273 Zhoujiazhui Road, suddenly disappeared while playing at the back door around 5 p.m. on October 6. Huang searched everywhere without success. Huang has only this one son and was extremely anxious. She posted a note at the entrance of the alley, stating that if someone returned the child, she would give 50 yuan and would not go back on her word. However, it was still ineffective. Huang could only weep and sob every day until an old woman came with a letter on the 9th of this month, saying that she had news of her child, who was near the Caojiadu Garden. It would cost 140 yuan to get him back. Huang was overjoyed upon hearing this. After lunch, she took the money and went to negotiate with the old woman and her brother-in-law, Huang Lao Si, according to the instructions. They waited for a long time, but no one came to negotiate. The old woman then excused herself and left by tram. Later that night, as it suddenly started to rain, a rickshaw slowly approached. Her son, Jin Lin, was sitting alone in the rickshaw. At that time, someone behind her shouted that she should put the money on the ground and take her son home from the rickshaw. Huang did as she was told, left the money, rushed forward, grabbed her son, hired a rickshaw, and returned home with her brother-in-law, Huang A'si. The pearl was returned to Hebu. According to reports, the Harbin police arrested a criminal in the case. The Western detective and Chinese detective Zhou Kaiwen arrested a criminal named Cao Zhigan from Jiangbei near the Ren Shou Li area of Caojiadu on the evening of the previous day and brought him to the police station. The police chief ordered him to be detained and sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court yesterday morning. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, presented the case and requested a postponement. The plaintiff, Huang Li, testified about the previous events. According to Wei Haosan, the rickshaw driver, on that evening, there were three men and two women at the entrance of Ren Shou Li in Caojiadu. The defendant was one of them and hired him to drive the rickshaw. The child was held by an old woman and boarded the rickshaw. The defendant and another man hired two other rickshaws to follow behind. They got off at the back door of Zhaofeng Garden. After a while, the plaintiff arrived and took the child away. The whereabouts of the other defendants and the old woman were unknown. Huang Lao Si testified that he and the plaintiff went together and waited until late at night when they heard someone say to put the money on the ground and the child was in the rickshaw and to quickly go and get him. However, he could not see the person's face clearly. The defendant completely denied the charges, saying that he had been working as a ticket collector at the Yangzhou Theater in the Fifth District of the Chinese area for many years and had no time to commit such a crime. Ge, the prosecutor, ordered the witness, the rickshaw driver Wei Hongsan, to come forward again to carefully examine the defendant's face, fearing that he had made a mistake, otherwise he would be punished for perjury. He also ordered the court attendant to turn on the lights. Wei carefully examined the defendant and replied that he was not mistaken. Prosecutor Ge ordered the defendant to be taken back into custody for further questioning at a later date.

### Li Chen, the Woman in the Case of Strangling Her Daughter-in-Law, Died of Illness 151

Li Qingfu, who resided at No. 666 Gordon Road, was formerly a Chinese police officer, No. 615, at the Gordon Road Police Station. Because his daughter-in-law died suddenly and was found to have been strangled, Li Qingfu, his wife Li Chen, and his sons Yu Long and Yu Kun were all suspected and were detained and interrogated by Chinese detective Shao Jingfan of the police station at the Special District Court. Recently, Li Chen became ill in the detention center and died. The body was sent to the Coroner's Office on Fielun Road. Prosecutor Guo Huai Pu of the Special Court went to the office yesterday morning to examine the body and ordered that it be handed over to the deceased's nephew, Chen Jinting, for burial. It is reported that the case is scheduled to be heard again on the morning of the 19th of this month.

### Verdict in the Yellow Croaker Case 152

Wang Fucai Fined 300 Yuan

Wang Fucai, a Ningbo native who was the chief stoker on the Xiefopai Mei ship, was arrested on the 30th of last month for inviting Li Zaichen (also a Ningbo native), the head of the Western waiters on the same ship, to Room 13 of the Mibo Hotel in the French Concession and using threats to demand 4,000 yuan that he should have received for bringing eight Cantonese guests with smuggled yellow croaker fish to the United States. The case was discovered and Wang was arrested by Chinese and Western detectives from the Hongkou Police Station and sent to the Special District Court along with the suspect Xu Li Hui, also from Ningbo. Both defendants hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend them. The details of the interrogation have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The interrogation has ended and the verdict was pending. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge Zhiqin presided over the Third Court and sentenced Wang Fucai to a fine of 300 yuan. If he failed to pay the fine, he would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the final verdict was determined to be reduced by two yuan for every day of detention. Xu Li Hui was found not guilty.

### A Record of the Autumn Chrysanthemum Exhibition of the Gardening Society 153

Extraordinarily Successful

The Shanghai Chinese and Western Gardening Society (SHANGHAI HORTICULTURAL SOCILTY), founded in 1875 by the British in the Municipal Council, initially limited its membership to Westerners. Later, people from various countries joined. In recent years, Chinese gentlemen from Shanghai, such as Hui Yuting and Ding Runxiang, joined as directors, and the scope of the society gradually expanded. It now has hundreds of members. The society holds competitions every spring and autumn and appoints judges. This year, Sir Peter Grain and Ding Hui served as judges and awarded prizes. The competition has been held at the Municipal Hall for many years. Last year, it was changed to the Dahua Hotel, which has a larger venue and more varieties of flowers. Ding also proposed that non-members be allowed to join the competition, which improved the results. Yesterday was the date of the society's Chrysanthemum Competition. The reporter took time to visit and saw various rare flowers and plants arranged in the room. Entering the room was like being in a fairyland. There were too many varieties to count. Some had flowers of several colors, and some had flowers as large as bowls. The flower stems were all four to five feet tall. The flower growers also competed to create various patterns with the flowers, which was a magnificent sight. Ding built two large flower towers, one with the letters S.H.S (the abbreviation of the society's Western name) and the other with two stars. It is said that Ding won two of the three first-place medals for the large flower towers. The other was won by the mistress of the Xinkang Garden. She also won the first prize for the six potted flower towers. The winners of the first prize for the scattered pots were the Westerner Mai Lai, the Deputy Chief of the Municipal Council Martin, and the Chinese Feng Bingnan and Li Bake. Ding also won the first, second, and third prizes for the scattered pots. In addition to chrysanthemums, there were also various agricultural products on display, classified into different categories. Ding's red peppers were five to six inches long and three to four inches in diameter. Lighting them up was truly like holding a candle at night, which was a rare sight. It is said that the seeds of the agricultural products came from abroad, but the products were larger and better than those from abroad. This was probably due to the fertile soil and proper cultivation. In short, the prosperity of the society today is due to the efforts of Ding, the directors, and the Chinese and Western members.

### The Finale of the Municipal Garden Chrysanthemum Exhibition 154

The lively scene of the Municipal Garden Chrysanthemum Exhibition has been repeatedly reported in previous newspapers. The last day of the exhibition happened to be the Prime Minister's birthday, a holiday for all sectors, so the number of visitors increased sharply. Huang Daolin, the section chief of the municipal government, came again to enjoy the exhibition for the second time. Shen Yi, the director of the Bureau of Public Works, and the teachers and students of Tongde and Tongji Medical Colleges also arrived successively. More than 30 male and female teachers and staff of Shanggong Elementary School also had a meal in the venue. Zhejiang University's Agricultural College, seeing that the venue had many famous chrysanthemums, specially sent Mr. Ji Zhuomin to request that some good varieties be shared. Shi Bumei, a painter from eastern Zhejiang, also brought writing utensils to sketch the chrysanthemums in preparation for making a catalog. Other celebrities brought cameras to photograph the chrysanthemums all day long. Until the setting sun, the ferries were about to stop, and there were still people reluctant to leave, which can be said to be a testament to the love of chrysanthemums. After the review committee completed the judging of the exhibits, it was heard that Xiaoguan Garden and Bixia Garden were the most outstanding, and the Public School Garden, Shen Xingyuan, Sanyou Industrial Society, Jinan University, and the Rural Normal School also scored well.

### The Pingyang Warship Damaged in Bandit Suppression 155

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday for Repairs

At around 8 a.m. yesterday morning, three large black pirate ships carrying 200 pirates were discovered outside the Wusong Estuary, attempting to loot five merchant ships anchored in the harbor. Gong Mianqin, the captain of the 17th Team of the 4th District of the Jiangsu Provincial Public Security Water Police, was leading the Pingyang gunboat on patrol in the waters off the Yemao Estuary. Seeing the situation, he immediately opened fire with fast cannons and machine guns at the pirate ships. The pirate ships also opened fire and resisted stubbornly. After about half an hour of fierce fighting, the pirate force was overwhelmed and hoisted sails to flee to the open sea. The Pingyang warship was hit by the pirate ships' gunfire, damaging the hull, steering room, stern, and wings, making it unable to pursue. The pirate ships escaped. The warship arrived in Shanghai yesterday for repairs.

### Appeal from the People of Zhu Zhai Due to Crop Failure 156

Zhu Zhai Town in the western suburbs of Shanghai, at the intersection of the three counties of Shang, Jia, and Qing, is an area where the people depend on agriculture for their livelihood. Cotton and soybeans are the main crops. This summer, due to uneven rainfall and a typhoon, the harvest was greatly reduced, and the farmers were worried. They have repeatedly appealed to the local authorities to request that Shanghai and Jiaqing counties send people to inspect the damage in order to reduce taxes. Shanghai Jiading sent people to inspect the damage a few days ago, but Qingpu County has not yet expressed any opinion. It was heard yesterday that local authorities have again submitted a request to the Qingpu County Government's Finance Bureau to send specialists to the countryside as soon as possible to inspect the disaster situation in order to alleviate the suffering of the people.

Continued Burial of Exposed Corpses at Pushan Villa 157

Mr. Wang Junsheng, Director of Pushan Villa, following the wishes of Mr. Wang Yiting, Chairman of the Joint Charity Organizations, has been handling the burial of exposed corpses in the areas bordering Jiangsu and Zhejiang for three years, burying a total of 29,713 bodies. However, he laments that there are still more than 100,000 corpses in various places that have not been collected and buried. This winter, the work will continue. Recently, he personally went to various parts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to discuss the matter. As the weather gradually turns cold and the west wind rises sharply, even the small bones among the corpses seem to feel the cold and burrow into the mud, which is truly pitiful. It can be seen that although humans are the most intelligent of all creatures, even their dead bones still know the warmth and cold of the seasons. Mr. Wang was heartbroken by the sight and rushed back to Shanghai to raise funds. He immediately notified Wangjiangjing, Wangdian, Jiaxing, Nanxun, Yanmu, Zhenze, Puyuan, Pinghu, and other places to start collecting and burying the corpses, so that those exposed can be laid to rest and the foul odor will not be carried by the wind, which is of great importance to public health in the area. It is hoped that the wealthy people of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, who are not lacking in benevolence, will hear of this and generously contribute to this good cause, which will truly bring immeasurable blessings.

Escaped After Being Caught, Sustained Gunshot Wound Due to Possession of Red Pills 159

As the winter season arrives, petty thieves are rampant. In order to reduce kidnapping and theft cases, the Concession authorities have ordered all police stations to instruct Chinese and Western detectives to search pedestrians along the way. The effect has been remarkable. At about 10:30 last night, detectives from the Laozha Police Station were searching pedestrians in the Zhengjia Wood Bridge area. A man named Zhao Siqing, 38 years old, from Jiangbei, who runs Hengji Rickshaw Company on Jiaxing Road, happened to have red pills hidden in his pocket. When he saw the detectives approaching, he ran away. The detectives suspected that he was hiding weapons and mistook him for a bandit, so they opened fire several times. Zhao was shot in the right shoulder, the bullet pierced his back, and he collapsed, bleeding profusely. He was then escorted to Renji Hospital for treatment by Western police officer No. 28 from the Laozha Police Station.

Miss Sheng Consumes Opium 160

Lying About Suddenly Suffering a Stroke

Miss Sheng, a young woman from Ningbo, aged 23, residing at No. 56 Xiafei Lane, Xiafei Road, in the French Concession, is beautiful and fashionably dressed. At about 9:00 AM yesterday, her family borrowed an ambulance from the Public Concession Municipal Council and took her to Baolong Hospital for treatment, falsely claiming that she had suddenly suffered a stroke. After examination, the Western doctor determined that she had undoubtedly consumed raw opium. She was given injections and stomach pumping, and her condition improved slightly, but due to excessive poisoning, she was still not out of danger late into the night. The reason for her suicide is still under investigation.

Conflict Between Workers and Russian Man, Police Station Accuses Chauffeur 161

Prosecuted for Aiding Others to Hinder Freedom

At around 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, a construction site near Bailinan Road and Yuyuan Road in West Shanghai saw a conflict between water and carpentry workers and a Russian foreman, Mr. Gordistin, over the calculation of wages. The workers hired a car to take Mr. Gordistin to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau, accompanied by the accountant and others from the construction site. After questioning by District Chief Ren, it was decided to refer the case to the Judicial Section of the General Bureau for review. This matter was reported yesterday. Bailinan Road was originally built by the Municipal Council beyond its boundaries, and the house being built is also located in the Chinese area. Therefore, after the conflict, the workers took Mr. Gordistin to the police station. The car was rented from the Wanguo Automobile Company on Yuyuan Road, license number 12519. The Jing'an Temple Police Station received a report and immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate the construction site, and arrested the chauffeur Cao Deyuan. Yesterday morning, the police station's lawyer filed a lawsuit against Cao, accusing him of helping others hinder Mr. Gordistin's freedom. The police escorted Cao to the Special District Court, and three witnesses, an Englishman Mr. Tenley, Mr. Talin, and an American Mr. Afang, testified in court. The defendant also hired lawyers Fan Gang and others to defend him. Judge Sun Yuan briefly questioned them and ordered Cao Deyuan to pay 2,000 yuan in bail and wait for the Public Security Bureau to bring the witnesses to court for further questioning. Besides the Russian Mr. Gordistin, Zhang Guirong, the accountant, Hua Guanhong, and Wang Asi, workers, are being detained at the Public Security Bureau. The names recorded in yesterday's report differ slightly.

Liu Yingzhou Imprisoned for Three Months 162

Liu Yingzhou, the main character in the case of the double suicide of mother and daughter, was sued by Zhou Qifeng, the younger brother of the deceased, at the District Court. The prosecutor filed a public prosecution on the charge of abandonment. After the Criminal Court concluded the debate, the judge studied the case and concluded that Liu Yingzhou's crime was proven, so yesterday he announced the verdict, sentencing Liu to three months imprisonment as a warning.

French Sailors Drunk and Stab Chinese 163

Two Seriously Injured, Three Slightly Injured

At about 9:00 PM on the 8th of this month, several workers were on their way home after work, passing in front of Qiming Girls' School on Tianyao Bridge. Some French sailors from the Catholic Church, drunk and in a group, used wine bottles in their hands to hit the workers. The workers were unable to avoid them and were hit on the head, bleeding profusely. They then pulled out knives and stabbed at them randomly, causing them to faint instantly. Two people were seriously injured (Ding Jiaqun and Luo Haiyou), and three were slightly injured. Liu Yunfang, the chief of the Second Precinct of the Sixth District, upon hearing the news, personally led the police to the scene. The French sailors immediately closed the iron gates of Qiming Girls' School and fired shots repeatedly. (According to reports, the French sailors were stationed inside the Qiming Girls' School established by the Catholic Church.) Chief Liu was not afraid and captured the French sailor who committed the crime, along with a cartridge case, and brought them back to the station. He sent the injured workers to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to his superiors for serious negotiations.

Puyi Society's New Building Completed 164

About to Open

The Puyi Society, a Christian organization on Zixia Road, Dadongmen, began construction of a new building last year, and the work has now been completed. It is scheduled to hold an opening ceremony on the 17th of this month and invite people from all walks of life to visit. The new building has five floors and covers an area of about one mu, costing 100,000 taels. The interior is equipped with the latest scientific equipment. It is the only large building in South Shanghai, with facilities such as men's and women's bathrooms, a gym, a grand hall, a billiard room, and a rooftop movie theater. After the opening ceremony, there will be string and piano ensembles by famous orchestras, and choral performances by all members of Shanghai's most famous Elegant Music Society.

A Comedic Scene 165

Concubine Formally Married, Leading to a Chaotic Brawl

Wei Chunsheng from Pudong, over forty years old, is engaged in the barge business and owns two docks and boats. He is now a deputy foreman of a barge company and is relatively wealthy. He is fond of carousing. His wife has already given birth to a son and daughter. Three years ago, Wei took a concubine. Recently, he became romantically involved with Yang Lanhua, a prostitute from a brothel in the French Concession. Lanhua is only in her early twenties, beautiful and charming. The two are deeply in love and have pledged to be together forever. Lanhua is unwilling to be a concubine, so Wei, infatuated with her beauty, agrees to formally marry her, agreeing to pay her family 700 yuan. The wedding was scheduled for the 20th, a few days ago. They rented a hall at a hotel on Avenue Edward VII, set up a wedding hall, prepared a wedding feast, and invited relatives and friends to a banquet. In the evening, they used a colorful sedan chair and ceremonial guards to bring Lanhua to the hotel. As the two were bowing to heaven and earth, red candles were burning high, and the hall was filled with joy, Wei's wife Zhu, along with her children and relatives, barged into the hotel and started a brawl. They knocked the flowers and candles on the platform to the ground. Zhu grabbed Lanhua and beat her severely. The colorful clothes, jeweled crown, glasses, and red veil worn by the bride were all torn off. Seeing that the situation was not good, Wei took the opportunity to escape through the back door of the hotel. With the persuasion of relatives and friends, Zhu and others were stopped, and Lanhua was released. The wedding hall was a chaotic mess. The relatives and friends were about to start feasting when they were suddenly dispersed, which was a great disappointment. Wei compensated for all the damaged clothes the next day, and the matter was settled.

Rotary Club Awards Waiting to be Claimed 166

The Rotary Club previously held a dance at the Dahua Hotel to raise funds for the Russian Volunteer School for Orphans and also held a lottery. However, more than 80 prizes won by those who purchased tickets have not yet been claimed. The Rotary Club has set a deadline of June 24 for claiming the awards. After this deadline, the prizes will be sold and the proceeds will be donated to the Russian Volunteer School for Orphans. The prize collection point is the Rotary Club office at No. 50 Nanjing Road.

Fire on Danshui Road 167

At 1:29 PM yesterday, a fire broke out in the loft of a new building along the road at No. 200 Danshui Road in the Public Concession. Smoke billowed through the roof, and the front of the building was completely destroyed, also affecting the neighboring building at No. 199. Fortunately, the fire brigade quickly arrived at the scene and worked hard to extinguish the fire, which was put out after half an hour.

Robbery in South Wharf Yesterday Morning 168

Wang Fengsheng, a resident of No. 23 Dachang Lane, Yangshou Alley, South Wharf, South Shanghai, works as an import goods tax inspector at the Railway Tax Bureau of the South Railway Station. At about 5:00 AM yesterday, six robbers suddenly came to his house. They were wearing short blue and black clothes and spoke with Shandong, Jiangbei, and Ningbo accents. One of the robbers held a letter and entered the house under the pretext of asking for someone. The other robbers followed and broke into the living room. Two robbers guarded the front and back doors, while four robbers went upstairs. Wang had not yet gotten out of bed but woke up upon hearing the noise. The robbers pointed a gun at him and said that they knew he was a well-known and came to borrow 2,000 yuan and told him to hand it over quickly. Unable to resist, Wang had to let them search and rob him. The robbers stole more than 400 yuan in cash, a pearl necklace, a pearl ring, a gold bracelet, a gold ring, a gem-inlaid ring, and a gold button, worth a total of about 400 yuan. After getting the loot, the robbers shouted and fled north. Wang then reported the robbery to the First Precinct of the First Sub-bureau of the Municipal Public Security Bureau and asked them to investigate.

Special Report

Municipal Government Revises Regulations on Road Construction Fees 171

The Municipal Government revised the Shanghai Road Construction Fee Regulations yesterday. The following is a special excerpt:

Revised Shanghai Road Construction Fee Regulations, Chapter 1: General Provisions, Article 1: For the purpose of opening or renovating roads and carrying out other ancillary projects in this city, road construction fees may be levied from landowners on both sides of the road in accordance with the provisions of these Regulations. Article 2: All land within the boundaries of this city, whether publicly or privately owned, shall be subject to the provisions of these Regulations. Article 3: The road construction fees levied under these Regulations shall be divided into two categories: project fees and land fees. (A) Project fees include construction of roads, ditches, bridges, culverts, etc., and costs of house demolition, etc. (B) Land fees include compensation for land acquired. Chapter 2: General Rules, Article 4: For roads that are opened or renovated at one time, project fees and land fees may be levied simultaneously. The amount and payment deadline shall be announced by the Municipal Government each time a road is built. Article 5: For roads that are not renovated at one time, project fees shall not be levied, and the land fees that landowners should pay according to Article 12 of these Regulations may be paid when a complete section between two roads is renovated. Article 6: The area used as the basis for levying fees shall be limited to those benefiting from the road construction. The standard shall be twice the prescribed width of the road, extending from the new road into both sides. In special circumstances, the Municipal Government may increase or decrease it at its discretion. Article 7: When neighboring roads are opened at the same time, resulting in overlapping fee ranges, the boundary of each road's fee zone shall be determined according to the following provisions: (A) The length of the land and frontage at the corner shall be bounded by the bisecting line of the intersection point of the two roads. (B) When the distance between the front and rear roads is too narrow, causing the overlapping of benefit ranges, the boundary shall be the dividing line of the overlapping part. (C) When roads are opened around the land at the same time, refer to the provisions in paragraphs A and B. Article 8: If land is within the benefit range prescribed in Article 6 of these Regulations, and there is no access road connecting to the new road, it shall not be considered as benefiting and no fees shall be levied. However, if the situation changes due to the transfer of property rights of the land before and after, the fees shall still be calculated and paid in accordance with the fee unit in Article 9 and the provisions in Article 12 of these Regulations, and the burden shall be borne by the heirs of the landowner. Chapter 3: Project Fees, Article 9: The calculation standard for levying project fees shall be based on dividing half of the total project fee levied according to the length of the frontage of the entire road, and the other half according to the amount of benefited area of the entire road, to obtain the fee unit, and then calculate the levy based on the frontage length and benefited area occupied by each household. Article 10: The levy of project fees shall be handled in accordance with the following provisions, but in special circumstances, the Municipal Government may increase or decrease them at its discretion: road width of 20 feet and below, levy 100% of the project fee; 25 feet, 80%; 30 feet, 60%; 35 feet and above, 40%. Article 11: If neighboring roads are opened in stages, the levy of project fees for roads opened later may be recalculated and offset according to the length of time between the openings in accordance with the provisions of Article 7 of these Regulations to levy the difference, or levied separately as usual, all of which shall be handled at the discretion of the Municipal Government. Chapter 4: Land Fees, Article 12: All land required for road construction shall be levied at 30% of the current market price of the benefited land on both sides. Chapter 5: Fee Procedures, Article 13: When paying compensation to landowners, the fees payable by the person receiving the compensation may be deducted. If it is insufficient, the landowner shall pay the full amount. Article 14: Landowners shall pay the fees in full within the prescribed time limit. The payment deadline for vacant land shall not exceed one year at most. The fees for building land must be paid before construction begins. Article 15: If landowners are unable to pay the fees, they may request the competent authority of the Municipal Government to purchase all or part of their land at the land price before the road was opened or renovated for compensation. If there is any remaining money, it shall be returned to the landowner. Article 16: If landowners fail to pay the fees in full within the time limit, it shall be regarded as tax arrears, and interest shall be levied on the amount owed at an annual rate of 5% from the date it should have been paid. Article 17: When the land price tax owed by landowners reaches the total amount of tax payable for three years, the competent authority of the Municipal Government may notify in writing 30 days in advance to auction all or part of the tax-defaulted land and its fixtures to the extent sufficient to offset the tax owed. If there is any remaining money, it shall be returned to the original tax debtor. Article 18: Landowners who can provide sufficient tax payment guarantee after receiving the notice in the preceding paragraph may have the auction postponed by the competent authority of the Municipal Government to show consideration. However, this postponement shall be limited to one year at most. Article 19: The road construction fees levied after the land price is announced in this city for the purpose of implementing land value increment tax shall be deducted when levying the increment tax. Chapter 6: Supplementary Provisions, Article 20: These Regulations may be revised at any time if there are any matters not covered. Article 21: These Regulations shall come into force on the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

A Laughing Matter 172

— Hai Ke

Young woman (coming out of a concert and meeting a tenor at the door)

— Mr., I listened to your earth-shattering singing today and I admire it very much.

Musician — You flatter me, you flatter me. Does Miss have any instructions?

Young woman — I can't find my car, and the chauffeur doesn't know where he's hiding. Could you possibly use your highest note to shout "Ah Gen"?

A — You are a famous advertising guru. The advertisements you write must be very effective.

B — How could they not be? The day before yesterday, I wrote an advertisement for a wealthy man to "Recruit a bodyguard Hercules" and posted it in the newspaper. He was kidnapped that day.

Pen seller — Sir, this fountain pen is a bit more expensive, but it is sturdy and durable. I guarantee you can use it for a lifetime.

Old gentleman — I am already over sixty years old and won’t need it for that many years. Please give me a pen that will last half a lifetime or a quarter of a lifetime.

Husband — Last night, when our child came home late, wasn't he drunk again?

Wife — I don't know if he was drunk, but after he came back, he asked me for a mirror to see who he was.

A Record of Exploring Doucui Rock 173

— Zhou Zixian

I started from Qujiang, Guangdong, through mountain paths. All I passed were towering mountains and steep ridges. I often walked for dozens of miles without seeing any human habitation. After walking for five days, I finally arrived at Dutou Si, forty miles south of Zixing County, Hunan Province. My colleague, Mr. Cao Xiangjing (a native of Zixing), told me, "There is a scenic spot here called Doucui Rock, which is about five miles away. Why don't you go for a visit?" I said, "Good." Mr. Cao said, "I have a teacher named Li who is currently in charge of the local defense bureau. We can invite him to come along as a guide." So, Mr. Li led the way for a visit. What I saw in the rock was of great research value. At that time, I recorded one or two things. Now, it has been almost three years since I came to Shanghai, and I can no longer remember them. I happened to read my old diary, and the scenes and circumstances are still vivid in my mind. I have specially recorded them here for geologists to explore.

At half past four that afternoon, Mr. Li hired a small boat. After boarding the boat, the river was narrow and the water was rapid, flowing downstream. In less than half an hour, I saw a high mountain towering into the clouds. Mr. Li pointed and said to me, "This is Doucui Rock." I went ashore and climbed up the stone steps. It took about half an hour to reach the summit. Although we were all healthy, we all felt tired. After a short rest, we summoned our remaining courage and continued to advance, finally reaching our destination. In front of the rock was an ancient temple, which was very clean. There were about dozens of monks. When they saw us suddenly arriving in military uniform, they were shocked and didn't know what to do. It turned out that no soldiers had ever visited this mountain. We asked them, and most of them were beggars from Sichuan who had been here for many years. After a short rest, I wanted to go inside and explore as soon as possible for the sake of enjoyment. Because the cave was as dark as pitch, a servant burned pine resin oil (because there was very little oxygen in the cave, so it was not easy to suffocate) to lead the way. As soon as I entered the cave, I saw smoke filling the air. There were several monks surrounding the Bodhi tree, chanting Buddhist scriptures incessantly. They were performing evening prayers. The inside of the cave was about two feet high from top to bottom and about three or four feet wide from front to back, like a house. To the right of the cave, there was a small spring gurgling. It was clear and sweet to drink. According to the servant, the spring water does not decrease if you take it, nor does it increase if you don't take it. It is available at all times of the year, and the wonders of physics are truly immeasurable. Behind the cave wall, there was a hole that could only be passed by a servant who led us into another large cave. The upper and lower parts of the cave were about four or five feet high. On the right, there were icicles hanging down like eaves, countless. Looking around, they were all red in color. The sound of striking them was as loud as a chime, which was also something that people could not bear to let go of. After passing through another small hole, there was another cave. On one side of the cave stood a stone tablet with the "Exploration Record of Doucui Rock" carved on it. I hurriedly did not take a closer look. Behind the tablet, there was a small cave. The servant said that this was the Immortal Cave. A monk from Sichuan came here one day, entered it, and never came out. It is said that he has become an immortal. We all wanted to enter, but the cave was extremely low, only four or five feet, or two or three feet, and we had to bend down and crawl down. When we reached the end of the cave, there was something like an earthen door. Looking inside, it was a small rectangular cave about five feet long, with a width and height of two feet. When we lit a torch, we saw a corpse lying there. The skull and cheekbones were still vaguely discernible. We retreated quickly, and then carefully recognized what was written on the tablet, which roughly said that this cave was in the Republic of China, year thirteen, when a famous person named Doucui entered the cave to explore. The fire he was holding suddenly went out. Fortunately, he had matches and lit it again, and then he discovered this relic. Therefore, it is said that there is an immortal in this cave who transformed here. I didn't believe this at the time. Perhaps someone curious wanted to explore the cave to its end, but there was no air inside, causing the fire to go out, and they could not get out and suffocated to death there. We were inside for three hours, and we were all exhausted and dared not go any further. So, we returned along the original route. When we came out, Mr. Li also said that before that, he and four or five friends had once ventured deep into it. One time, they entered the cave with fire at about four o'clock in the afternoon, passed through one cave and came out of another, and were even more timid and exhausted, and there was still no end. By the time they came out of the cave, it was already eight o'clock the next morning. He spoke as if he were talking about a tiger with a broken string. That night, we all stayed in the temple and had a vegetarian meal. At dawn, we saw the steep cliffs behind the mountain standing tall and impassable. There were no other high mountains nearby. I recalled where the spring water inside the rock came from, and why there were so many caves. The changes in the earth's crust are so profound that they cannot be measured. It is a pity that this mountain is unfortunately located in such a remote area. If it were in prosperous places such as Guangzhou or Shanghai, and artificial repairs were carried out to open it up with tunnels, install electric lights, and make the air circulate and have light, then tourists would follow one after another. The name of Doucui Rock should also be spread far and wide.

Hao Shuchen's Peach Blossom Village 174

— Chongliang

Hao Shuchen's newly staged "Peach Blossom Village" is taken from the story of Lu Zhishen Drunkenly Beating the Little Overlord in "Water Margin". It was compiled by my friend Wu Huansun, the host of the Yinbi Hall. This humorous comedy has long been famous in Pingjin. Shuchen once used this play and "Flying Tiger Dream" (Niu Gao's Marriage Recruitment at Ouhangguan) as a means of attracting audiences when he was a pillar performer in Tianjin, opening a new era for pure clowns to support a troupe alone. Its box office success was not weak, which shows its excellence. This time, Shuchen came south, and because there were too many roles in the troupe, the plays were not easy to distribute. It was not until last week that it was posted for performance. The audience praised it highly. The night before, it was performed for the second time. The reporter made a special trip to visit. I first met Shuchen backstage. Everyone advised Hao Da not to stick to the example of Lu Zhishen's bare chest and abdomen because of the sudden cold weather these days. Hao said that if he removed this costume, he would lose the original character of the rough monk. Moreover, the most taboo thing about acting is laziness, so he was unwilling to be lazy. From this, it can be seen that Shuchen is serious about everything. This play focuses on acting, reciting, teasing, and singing. Most of the singing is fragmented and not complicated. Shuchen's reputation for reciting plays with good timbre, pure charm, sufficient transmission of spirit, and clear pronunciation has been established for a long time. Watching his appearance and self-introduction, as well as the large section of dialogue about pretending to be a Buddha to deceive food, can be described as perfectly integrated with divine inspiration, humorous and witty, and most able to arouse the audience's interest. The scene of dressing up as a woman in the bridal chamber does not fall into the stereotype of Li Kui in Qingfeng Village. From head to toe, he completely changes into women's clothing, waiting for the Little Overlord to answer questions in the bridal chamber one by one by throwing them out of the tent to strengthen his belief and add humor. The compiler's ability to innovate and bring forth new ideas is truly ingenious and insightful. When advising the Little Overlord, he uses his own experience to show the great purpose of transforming evil and improving goodness, which is very appropriate, and clearly outlines the entire play, attributing the report to correcting people's hearts. This play is indeed not a fictional story. Yang Sili was a popular actor more than ten years ago, but now he is down and out. His voice is still sweet and round. The tricks he plays have unexpected twists and turns. Because of his background as a martial clown, he plays the Little Overlord with a crisp recitation that is superior to others. The tumbling and jumping in the bridal chamber battle are very skilled. It is conceivable that Zhu Guangzu, who stole hooks in the Chain Trick, can still be picked up. Now that there is Shuchen's Dou Erdun and Ruian's Huang Tianba, why not rehearse it once? In the play, when the Little Overlord takes a sedan chair to welcome the bride, he uses Suona to compose new lyrics and sing the Great Repair Vat tune. Also, the Great King is forced by Lu Zhishen to imitate the undressing of a porter. The two scenes are interspersed and are quite lively. The compiler can be said to be good at using play materials.

Dwarf Island 175

— Ji Jin

A certain number of miles from the northern coast of Africa is what is known as the Tim Ers Island, commonly known as Dwarf Island. The natives there are short in stature, only two feet from head to toe, with yellow skin and black faces, no different from the Inuit people of North America. However, due to their remote location and inconvenient transportation overseas, few Europeans and Americans have been able to reach their land. This summer, the British explorer Mr. Darley ventured to go there to learn about the internal situation and quickly recorded it to provide assistance for conversation.

The dwarves live a simple life, eating dairy and meat, wearing fur, living under the sky and on the earth, with no fixed residence, just like a primitive tribe. However, they like to raise dogs. Wherever they go, they have hundreds of dogs, or at least dozens. When hunting, they guide the dogs forward, and then they carry bows and arrows to follow. The bow is no more than a foot long, and the arrow is only an inch long. The upper end is glued with poison. If they encounter a fierce beast, they draw the bow and shoot it. The arrow enters the beast's eye, and the poison takes effect and it falls to the ground. Then they order the dogs to drag it away. There are many wild birds and beasts on the island. In addition to hunting beasts, the dwarves are also good at catching birds. Their method is similar to the previous one. Swans and wild ducks are often used to feed the dogs. The dogs are fat and big, not inferior to European products. It is common to see them barking and biting wildly at strangers. Cowardly people have no choice but to retreat. When Mr. Da first arrived, he brought a lot of meat to feed the dogs. The dogs were too busy fighting for food, so he was able to go deep into the inland. When the dwarves saw him, they were greatly surprised, thinking that a god had descended from the sky. They bowed down and prostrated themselves, murmuring something unknown. Mr. Da then took out bread, melons and fruits to give to them and returned home overnight. It is said that he brought back a lot of rare birds and animals.

Short Message: The Shanghai Flower Planting Association held a chrysanthemum convention yesterday at the Dahua Hotel. Chinese and Western people with a love of flowers displayed their famous varieties of chrysanthemums in the meeting, supplemented by other exotic flowers, plants, fruits and vegetables, which were bizarre and dazzling. The beauty of the layout was especially unprecedented. Among the products of our country, Mr. Ding Runxiang, Gu Lanzhou, and Li Bake all won awards. Especially Mr. Ding's products were numerous. The chrysanthemums were so fat, beautiful and extraordinary that they could not be described. Some of them were decorated with flower buds to form Western characters, so they won the top two awards. Many visitors praised them incessantly.

A Brief Account of the Chinese Quarter in San Francisco (Part 2) 176

— Kang Kang

Guilds, public offices, schools, and clubs are mostly located on Stockton Street. The Chinese Guildhall, the Chinese Overseas School, the Tongyuan Association, the Kuomintang, the Constitutionalist Party, the Zhigongtang, the Youth Association, and the new and old churches all face each other. There are six Chinese newspapers in the Chinese Quarter: "Young China," which is the Kuomintang government's official newspaper; "National Public Daily," which is the Kuomintang's left-wing newspaper; "World Daily," which is the Constitutionalist Party's newspaper; "Gonglun Morning Post," which is the Zhigongtang's newspaper; "China and West Daily," which is the Christian church's newspaper; and "Jinshan Times," which is the American-born Chinese Association's newspaper. They are all not far apart, and each newspaper publishes two to three thousand copies.

The city government specially built a primary school for overseas Chinese near Stockton Street. The students are divided into classes totaling more than 1,500 people, which is the largest number of students in the city. The principal is an American teacher. Since last year, there have been two American-born Chinese women who have graduated from the California Normal School. Chinese children above middle school age can study with Americans, so there are no specially built schools. The original overseas Chinese were divided into six guildhalls according to their respective towns, but later they jointly organized the Chinese Guildhall. Each guildhall is attached to a primary school. The Chinese Guildhall has three levels of junior high school. All of them focus on Chinese studies and use textbooks published in the mainland. Boys and girls are in the same class. Classes are held every evening from 5:00 to 8:00. Each school has at least 100 people, and some have as many as 400 to 500 people. In the past 30 years, American immigration regulations have become increasingly harsh, and the number of overseas Chinese has sharply decreased. Fortunately, the number of American-born children has increased, and their educational progress has also been quite advanced. The future is immeasurable.

The overseas Chinese are all Cantonese, and their lifestyles and customs are the same as those in the mainland. Men do not all wear Western clothes, but they all wear short coats. Women wear a mix of Chinese and Western clothing, taking a compromise. Entertainment includes food, drink, singing, dancing, and gambling. The streets are especially bustling and lively at night, with a constant stream of pedestrians and customers filling the seats at late-night snacks. The sound of wind and string instruments can also be heard from time to time, but according to custom, they do not dare to drink heavily and get drunk. Westerners come to the Chinese Quarter to visit in an endless stream. There are sightseeing buses and local guides and interpreters. On average, there are three to four hundred people every day. The Youth Association has specially set up a reception center. The Chinese Quarter of San Francisco is actually the only model residential area for Chinese people in the New World. Although there are many overseas Chinese in cities such as New York, Chicago, and Philadelphia, they are scattered in various places and are far from being comparable to this.

Warmth in My Heart (314) 177

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 15: Tears Fall on All Sides in Sadness of Red Love, a Seat Leans Inward in Lingering Green Intent

It turned out that Ling Zhixiang had several wives at home. They didn't all live in one place. He would rather walk a little himself, coming here today and going there tomorrow. He had his palaces everywhere. He said that under the rule of a man, there simply cannot be two factions of women. Women are really like tigers. When two tigers fight, one will definitely be injured. If two women share one man, they will have to fight to the death. As the saying goes, one bowl doesn't ring, but two bowls clang. This is not wrong. Living in different places, although it is a bit of labor to run east and west, it is more peaceful in spirit. Otherwise, living in one place, quarreling morning and night, is a common thing among adult gentlemen and families, and is not surprising. But it still brings a kind of unhappiness to people's spirits. Therefore, he has all the wives living in one place, and those who live in one house have to be ranked as the first wife, the second wife, and the third wife. Those who live separately naturally have a good way to make them all equal. Do you know what it is? People are named after the place they live. For example, those who live on Mahou Road are called Mahou Road Wife, and those who live on Kader Road are called Kader Road Wife. Those who live on Malang Road and Baochang Road are called Malang Road and Baochang Road Wife, just like the Shandong governor and Henan governor in the warlord era, who are all called after the place names, or like the Hefei chancellor and Nanpi minister in the former Qing dynasty. Their place names were used as general names. Later, after people got used to calling them Mahou Road Wife and Kader Road Wife, they removed the word "Wife" and simply called them Mahou Road and Kader Road. They called each other Mahou Road said this and that, and Kader Road said this and that. Mahou Road can stand up and speak, which is like a joke. In fact, this is just a habit and is not surprising. Fortunately, they each guard their own territory and do not invade the boundary. If people don't offend me, I won't offend them. As long as Mahou Road doesn't go to Kader Road to quarrel, and Kader Road doesn't go to Mahou Road to scold, they can live in peace. As for their own demands, those who have a little nagging and chattering, as long as they are handled properly, there is always a way. Ordinary women can be dealt with by using a little emotionalism and massage-style diplomacy. The first thing is not to let the two sides meet. After meeting, things will gradually happen, and even conflict with each other. He is a polygamous family. The policy for dealing with polygamous families is this, so people often ask him what the secret is for a man with one wife and one concubine to be fine all day long from morning to night and from night to morning, making the man feel embarrassed. Sometimes both sides want to detain him, and sometimes both sides reject him. Seeing that Ling Zhixiang has five or six wives and is always okay, people often ask him what the secret is.

Financial Gold Standard Reversal and Decline 178

The swap spread had been near, and market sentiment was slightly weak. Yesterday, the 13th, the gold standard slightly declined again. However, the state was peaceful, and the unified daily turnover was only a few taels of silver. Looking back, the amount of intraday trading was only slightly more than one tael. Foreign exchange was also weak and clumsy. Demand from fellow traders was scarce. As for the buying and selling of various firms, Yongheng bought a considerable amount, speculated by Luo, who shorted. Zhifeng, Yongyuanmao, Yongfuchang, and others were mostly sellers. The early market seemed slightly lower. The overseas silver market only showed a slight drop in large bars. The price of silver did not change further, and because the exchange rate fell, people's hearts were empty. Later, the sellers were overwhelmed, and suddenly the 90-tael mark was broken. Afterwards, Yuancheng, Yongyuanmao, Yongheng, and others continued to buy, but the Dalian gang and retail investors mostly sold out due to swap spreads or fears of a large increase. Therefore, the market price broke through 90 taels again. The short sellers were under strong bullish pressure, and the environment was forcing them to be stimulated. Afterwards, many sellers rushed in, especially as the exchange rate did not improve but loosened. The bank sold January English gold at 173.125, and suddenly the market turned downward, re-entering the 90-tael range. The following is a detailed record of the situation before and after the market.

Hovering around 90 taels. The opening price in the morning of December was 590 taels, a drop of 9 qian and 1 mao. The market was calculated at 89 taels. There were many buyers around 90 taels, probably because the large bar was down another 1/16, but the price of silver did not move. The British and Japanese exchange rates were down by 32/1, and the Japanese and American exchange rates were down by 16/1, so the market sentiment was weak. Then it fell another 3 or 4 qian, but Yongheng vigorously covered its shorts, so it was pulled up by a few qian to 90 taels and 3 qian. Yuancheng and Yongfuchang sold, and the sentiment in the market was poor, so it was difficult to sustain. The 90-tael mark was suddenly broken, only to 88 taels and 3 qian. As for bill transactions, only Dalian bills were absorbed by Mitsui, recently at 1 tael, 2 qian, 7 fen, and 625 hao, and it was not easy to sell. When the advance order was announced, the listed price was 88 taels, 8 or 9 qian, and there was no change. It fell again to 8 taels, 3 or 4 qian. The internal exchange rates were flat. Korea sold spot dollars at 38.875 yuan, which was bought by silver companies. Taiwan bought spot Dalian at 1 tael, 2 qian, 7 fen, and 5625 hao. The price of gold was around 89 taels. After 10:45, the trend seemed to be high, mostly because Yuancheng, Yongheng, and hedgers chased in, and the price rose by 1 tael. Sumitomo bought February English gold at 173.125. Zhongfu and Dongya mutually traded January prices. At 11:15, it rose to 89 taels and 9 qian, but Zhifeng, Yongyuanmao, Yong, and retail investors sold out. Suddenly, it fell by 1 tael to 8 taels and 9 qian. Soon, it rebounded by 3 or 4 qian. At noon closing, it was 8 taels and 8 qian. The December English gold was traded between banks at 1725. Afterwards, there was a slight transaction of 4 or 5 qian, and the quoted price was still 623 taels and 4 qian, a discount of 34 or 5 taels.

The final result was a drop of 2 taels and 4 qian. The after-market opened at 89 taels and 3 qian, already up by 4 or 5 qian, because Yongheng still had buying. Then Yuancheng and others followed suit, and the price was pushed to 90 taels and 7 qian, then retreated by 8 or 9 qian. After 1:30, Taixing and Dadecheng entered the market, and buying gradually increased. It rose by 1 tael. At 3:00, it reached 91 taels, but there were few transactions at this price. In a blink of an eye, it fell by a few qian, because the bulls raised the price and released air, and the swap spread had to be 5 or 6 taels, which was enough to make the shorts feel cold, so they had to cover. However, bank drafts could still be supplied. Anda and Huabi did 1725 for November, and Huabi Bank sold 173.125 for January. However, there was little entanglement in the industry. Later, there seemed to be more sellers on the table. At 3:30, it fell to 89 taels and 2 qian, hovering around 90 taels. Around 4:00, Zhifeng, Yongtai, Kangrun, Yifeng, Yong, and others sold, so it plummeted by 1 tael and 6 or 7 qian. At 4:20, it was 88 taels and 4 qian. At the 4:30 closing, it was 88 taels and 5 qian, a drop of 2 taels and 4 qian compared to the previous day, which was a reversal of the three-day rise. The highest price of the day was 91 taels, and the lowest price was 88 taels and 3 qian, a difference of 2 taels and 7 qian.
